dotenv-expand [![NPM version](https://img.shields.io/npm/v/dotenv-expand.svg?style=flat-square)](https://www.npmjs.com/package/dotenv-expand)\\n40: \\n41: <img src=\\\"https://raw.githubusercontent.com/motdotla/dotenv-expand/master/dotenv-expand.png\\\" alt=\\\"dotenv-expand\\\" align=\\\"right\\\" width=\\\"200\\\" />\\n42: \\n43: Dotenv-expand adds variable expansion on top of [dotenv](http://github.com/motdotla/dotenv). If you find yourself needing to expand environment variables already existing on your machine, then dotenv-expand is your tool.\\n44: \\n45: [![js-standard-style](https://img.shields.io/badge/code%20style-standard-brightgreen.svg?style=flat-square)](https://github.com/feross/standard)\\n46: [![LICENSE](https://img.shields.io/github/license/motdotla/dotenv-expand.svg)](LICENSE)\\n47: [![codecov](https://codecov.io/gh/motdotla/dotenv-expand/graph/badge.svg?token=pawWEyaMfg)](https://codecov.io/gh/motdotla/dotenv-expand)\\n48: \\n49: ## Install\\n50: \\n51: ```bash\\n52: # Install locally (recommended)\\n53: npm install dotenv-expand --save\\n54: ```\\n55: \\n56: Or installing with yarn? `yarn add dotenv-expand`\\n57: \\n58: ## Usage\\n59: \\n60: Create a `.env` file in the root of your project:\\n61: \\n62: ```dosini\\n63: PASSWORD=\\\"s1mpl3\\\"\\n64: DB_PASS=$PASSWORD\\n65: ```\\n66: \\n67: As early as possible in your application, import and configure dotenv and then expand dotenv:\\n68: \\n69: ```javascript\\n70: const dotenv = require('dotenv')\\n71: const dotenvExpand = require('dotenv-expand')\\n72: \\n73: dotenvExpand.expand(dotenv.config())\\n74: \\n75: console.log(process.env) // remove this after you've confirmed it is expanding\\n76: ```\\n77: \\n78: That's it. `process.env` now has the expanded keys and values you defined in your `.env` file.\\n79: \\n80: ```\\n81: dotenvExpand.expand(dotenv.config())\\n82: \\n83: ...\\n84: \\n85: connectdb(process.env.DB_PASS)\\n86: ```\\n87: \\n88: ### Preload\\n89: \\n90: > Note: Consider using [`dotenvx`](https://github.com/dotenvx/dotenvx) instead of preloading. I am now doing (and recommending) so.\\n91: > \\n92: > It serves the same purpose (you do not need to require and load dotenv), has built-in expansion support, adds better debugging, and works with ANY language, framework, or platform. â€“ [motdotla](https://github.com/motdotla)\\n93: \\n94: You can use the `--require` (`-r`) [command line option](https://nodejs.org/api/cli.html#cli_r_require_module) to preload dotenv & dotenv-expand. By doing this, you do not need to require and load dotenv or dotenv-expand in your application code. This is the preferred approach when using `import` instead of `require`.\\n95: \\n96: ```bash\\n97: $ node -r dotenv-expand/config your_script.js\\n98: ```\\n99: \\n100: The configuration options below are supported as command line arguments in the format `dotenv_config_<option>=value`\\n101: \\n102: ```bash\\n103: $ node -r dotenv-expand/config your_script.js dotenv_config_path=/custom/path/to/your/env/vars\\n104: ```\\n105: \\n106: Additionally, you can use environment variables to set configuration options. Command line arguments will precede these.\\n107: \\n108: ```bash\\n109: $ DOTENV_CONFIG_<OPTION>=value node -r dotenv-expand/config your_script.js\\n110: ```\\n111: \\n112: ```bash\\n113: $ DOTENV_CONFIG_ENCODING=latin1 node -r dotenv-expand/config your_script.js dotenv_config_path=/custom/path/to/.env\\n114: ```\\n115: \\n116: ## Examples\\n117: \\n118: See [tests/.env.test](https://github.com/motdotla/dotenv-expand/blob/master/tests/.env.test) for simple and complex examples of variable expansion in your `.env`\\n119: file.\\n120: \\n121: ## Documentation\\n122: \\n123: `dotenv-expand` exposes one function:\\n124: \\n125: * expand\\n126: \\n127: ### Expand\\n128: \\n129: `expand` will expand your environment variables.\\n130: \\n131: ```js\\n132: const env = {\\n133:   parsed: {\\n134:     BASIC: 'basic',\\n135:     BASIC_EXPAND: '${BASIC}',\\n136:     BASIC_EXPAND_SIMPLE: '$BASIC'\\n137:   }\\n138: }\\n139: \\n140: console.log(dotenvExpand.expand(env))\\n141: ```\\n142: \\n143: #### Options\\n144: \\n145: ##### processEnv\\n146: \\n147: Default: `process.env`\\n148: \\n149: Specify an object to write your secrets to. Defaults to `process.env` environment variables.\\n150: \\n151: ```js\\n152: const myEnv = {}\\n153: const env = {\\n154:   processEnv: myEnv,\\n155:   parsed: {\\n156:     HELLO: 'World'\\n157:   }\\n158: }\\n159: dotenvExpand.expand(env)\\n160: \\n161: console.log(myEnv.HELLO) // World\\n162: console.log(process.env.HELLO) // undefined\\n163: ```\\n164: \\n165: ## FAQ\\n166: \\n167: ### What rules does the expansion engine follow?\\n168: \\n169: See a full list of rules [here](https://dotenvx.com/docs/env-file#interpolation).\\n170: \\n171: ### How can I avoid expanding pre-existing envs (already in my `process.env`, for example `pas$word`)?\\n172: \\n173: As of `v12.0.0` dotenv-expand no longer expands `process.env`.\\n174: \\n175: If you need this ability, use [dotenvx](https://github.com/dotenvx/dotenvx) by shipping an encrypted .env file with your code - allowing safe expansion at runtime.\\n176: \\n177: ### How can I override an existing environment variable?\\n178: \\n179: Use [dotenvx](https://github.com/dotenvx/dotenvx) as dotenv-expand does not support this.\\n180: \\n181: dotenv-expand is a separate module (without knowledge of the loading of `process.env` and the `.env` file) and so cannot reliably know what to override.\\n182: \\n183: ## Contributing Guide\\n184: \\n185: See [CONTRIBUTING.md](CONTRIBUTING.md)\\n186: \\n187: ## CHANGELOG\\n188: \\n189: See [CHANGELOG.md](CHANGELOG.md)\\n190: \\n191: ## Who's using dotenv-expand?\\n192: \\n193: [These npm modules depend on it.](https://www.npmjs.com/browse/depended/dotenv-expand)\\n194: <br>\n27: <a href=\"https://workos.com/?utm_campaign=github_repo&utm_medium=referral&utm_content=dotenv&utm_source=github\">\n28:   <div>\n29:     <img src=\"https://res.cloudinary.com/dotenv-org/image/upload/c_scale,w_400/v1665605496/68747470733a2f2f73696e647265736f726875732e636f6d2f6173736574732f7468616e6b732f776f726b6f732d6c6f676f2d77686974652d62672e737667_zdmsbu.svg\" width=\"270\" alt=\"WorkOS\">\n30:   </div>\n31:   <b>Your App, Enterprise Ready.</b>\n32:   <div>\n33:     <sup>Add Single Sign-On, Multi-Factor Auth, and more, in minutes instead of months.</sup>\n34:   </div>\n35: </a>\n36: <hr>\n37: </div>\n38: \n39: # dotenv-expand [![NPM version](https://img.shields.io/npm/v/dotenv-expand.svg?style=flat-square)](https://www.npmjs.com/package/dotenv-expand)\n40: \n41: <img src=\"https://raw.githubusercontent.com/motdotla/dotenv-expand/master/dotenv-expand.png\" alt=\"dotenv-expand\" align=\"right\" width=\"200\" />\n42: \n43: Dotenv-expand adds variable expansion on top of [dotenv](http://github.com/motdotla/dotenv). If you find yourself needing to expand environment variables already existing on your machine, then dotenv-expand is your tool.\n44: \n45: [![js-standard-style](https://img.shields.io/badge/code%20style-standard-brightgreen.svg?style=flat-square)](https://github.com/feross/standard)\n46: [![LICENSE](https://img.shields.io/github/license/motdotla/dotenv-expand.svg)](LICENSE)\n47: [![codecov](https://codecov.io/gh/motdotla/dotenv-expand/graph/badge.svg?token=pawWEyaMfg)](https://codecov.io/gh/motdotla/dotenv-expand)\n48: \n49: ## Install\n50: \n51: ```bash\n52: # Install locally (recommended)\n53: npm install dotenv-expand --save\n54: ```\n55: \n56: Or installing with yarn? `yarn add dotenv-expand`\n57: \n58: ## Usage\n59: \n60: Create a `.env` file in the root of your project:\n61: \n62: ```dosini\n63: PASSWORD=\"s1mpl3\"\n64: DB_PASS=$PASSWORD\n65: ```\n66: \n67: As early as possible in your application, import and configure dotenv and then expand dotenv:\n68: \n69: ```javascript\n70: const dotenv = require('dotenv')\n71: const dotenvExpand = require('dotenv-expand')\n72: \n73: dotenvExpand.expand(dotenv.config())\n74: \n75: console.log(process.env) // remove this after you've confirmed it is expanding\n76: ```\n77: \n78: That's it. `process.env` now has the expanded keys and values you defined in your `.env` file.\n79: \n80: ```\n81: dotenvExpand.expand(dotenv.config())\n82: \n83: ...\n84: \n85: connectdb(process.env.DB_PASS)\n86: ```\n87: \n88: ### Preload\n89: \n90: > Note: Consider using [`dotenvx`](https://github.com/dotenvx/dotenvx) instead of preloading. I am now doing (and recommending) so.\n91: > \n92: > It serves the same purpose (you do not need to require and load dotenv), has built-in expansion support, adds better debugging, and works with ANY language, framework, or platform. â€“ [motdotla](https://github.com/motdotla)\n93: \n94: You can use the `--require` (`-r`) [command line option](https://nodejs.org/api/cli.html#cli_r_require_module) to preload dotenv & dotenv-expand. By doing this, you do not need to require and load dotenv or dotenv-expand in your application code. This is the preferred approach when using `import` instead of `require`.\n95: \n96: ```bash\n97: $ node -r dotenv-expand/config your_script.js\n98: ```\n99: \n100: The configuration options below are supported as command line arguments in the format `dotenv_config_<option>=value`\n101: \n102: ```bash\n103: $ node -r dotenv-expand/config your_script.js dotenv_config_path=/custom/path/to/your/env/vars\n104: ```\n105: \n106: Additionally, you can use environment variables to set configuration options. Command line arguments will precede these.\n107: \n108: ```bash\n109: $ DOTENV_CONFIG_<OPTION>=value node -r dotenv-expand/config your_script.js\n110: ```\n111: \n112: ```bash\n113: $ DOTENV_CONFIG_ENCODING=latin1 node -r dotenv-expand/config your_script.js dotenv_config_path=/custom/path/to/.env\n114: ```\n115: \n116: ## Examples\n117: \n118: See [tests/.env.test](https://github.com/motdotla/dotenv-expand/blob/master/tests/.env.test) for simple and complex examples of variable expansion in your `.env`\n119: file.\n120: \n121: ## Documentation\n122: \n123: `dotenv-expand` exposes one function:\n124: \n125: * expand\n126: \n127: ### Expand\n128: \n129: `expand` will expand your environment variables.\n130: \n131: ```js\n132: const env = {\n133:   parsed: {\n134:     BASIC: 'basic',\n135:     BASIC_EXPAND: '${BASIC}',\n136:     BASIC_EXPAND_SIMPLE: '$BASIC'\n137:   }\n138: }\n139: \n140: console.log(dotenvExpand.expand(env))\n141: ```\n142: \n143: #### Options\n144: \n145: ##### processEnv\n146: \n147: Default: `process.env`\n148: \n149: Specify an object to write your secrets to. Defaults to `process.env` environment variables.\n150: \n151: ```js\n152: const myEnv = {}\n153: const env = {\n154:   processEnv: myEnv,\n155:   parsed: {\n156:     HELLO: 'World'\n157:   }\n158: }\n159: dotenvExpand.expand(env)\n160: \n161: console.log(myEnv.HELLO) // World\n162: console.log(process.env.HELLO) // undefined\n163: ```\n164: \n165: ## FAQ\n166: \n167: ### What rules does the expansion engine follow?\n168: \n169: See a full list of rules [here](https://dotenvx.com/docs/env-file#interpolation).\n170: \n171: ### How can I avoid expanding pre-existing envs (already in my `process.env`, for example `pas$word`)?\n172: \n173: As of `v12.0.0` dotenv-expand no longer expands `process.env`.\n174: \n175: If you need this ability, use [dotenvx](https://github.com/dotenvx/dotenvx) by shipping an encrypted .env file with your code - allowing safe expansion at runtime.\n176: \n177: ### How can I override an existing environment variable?\n178: \n179: Use [dotenvx](https://github.com/dotenvx/dotenvx) as dotenv-expand does not support this.\n180: \n181: dotenv-expand is a separate module (without knowledge of the loading of `process.env` and the `.env` file) and so cannot reliably know what to override.\n182: \n183: ## Contributing Guide\n184: \n185: See [CONTRIBUTING.md](CONTRIBUTING.md)\n186: \n187: ## CHANGELOG\n188: \n189: See [CHANGELOG.md](CHANGELOG.md)\n190: \n191: ## Who's using dotenv-expand?\n192: \n193: [These npm modules depend on it.](https://www.npmjs.com/browse/depended/dotenv-expand)\n194: ","url":"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/dotenv-expand--dibench@f59d9bf04ecbb1f2d5bdcf4ec5dacaf07359c1df/-/blob/README.md"}}}
